### Error Diagnosis

1.  **`log.blockMesh` Error: "Block ... has inward-pointing faces"**
    *   **Cause:** The `blockMeshDict` file defines two hexahedral blocks that share the same set of vertices but in a different order (e.g., `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)` and `hex (1 0 5 4 9 8 11 10)`). In OpenFOAM, the order of vertices determines the orientation of the block. When two blocks occupy the same physical space with inverted vertex ordering, they are considered to have "inward-pointing faces" (or overlapping/invalid topology), causing `blockMesh` to fail.
    *   **Context:** The provided `blockMeshDict` contains duplicate blocks for the same geometric region, likely a copy-paste error where the vertex order was reversed for the second block definition.

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
Based on the provided error logs and the user's requirement to use a specific geometry (3D square bend) with a start time of 0 and end time of 500, here is the diagnosis and the specific solution.

### Error Diagnosis

1.  **`log.blockMesh` Error: "Block ... has inward-pointing faces"**
    *   **Cause:** The `blockMeshDict` file defines two hexahedral blocks that share the same physical volume but have **inconsistent vertex ordering**. In OpenFOAM, the order of vertices in a `hex` definition determines the orientation of the cell faces. If two blocks overlap but have opposite winding orders (e.g., `0 1 4 5` vs `5 4 1 0`), OpenFOAM interprets this as one block having faces pointing "inward" into the other, which is a topological error.
    *   **Specifics in your file:** The file defines `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)` and `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)`. While these look like adjacent blocks, the vertex indices provided in the `vertices` list and the `blocks` list in your provided file content appear to create a geometry where the blocks are defined in a way that causes self-intersection or inverted faces relative to the defined coordinate system (specifically the `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)` block). The error message `4(5 11 10 4)` indicates a specific face on the second block is oriented incorrectly.
    *   **Root Cause:** The vertex ordering in the `blocks` section does not match the geometric reality of the `vertices` list for a valid 3D mesh. The vertices are defined such that the blocks overlap or are twisted.

2.  **`log.rhoSimpleFoam` Error: "Cannot find file 'points'"**
    *   **Cause:** This is a direct consequence of the `blockMesh` failure. Since the mesh generation failed, the `polyMesh` directory was not created, and the `points` file (which contains the mesh coordinates) is missing. The solver cannot run without a mesh.

### Proposed Solutions

To resolve the "inward-pointing faces" error and generate the mesh correctly, you must correct the `blockMeshDict` file. The current definition attempts to create a square bend but fails due to vertex ordering.

**1. Correct the `blockMeshDict` Geometry**
The provided `blockMeshDict` in the file list contains a geometry definition that results in invalid blocks. You need to redefine the `blocks` section to ensure the vertices form a valid, non-overlapping hexahedral mesh that represents the square bend.

The current file has two blocks that likely overlap or are defined with incorrect winding. The solution is to define the geometry as a single continuous block or two adjacent blocks with correct vertex ordering.

**Action:** Replace the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` with the following corrected definition. This definition creates a single block that represents the bent geometry by correctly ordering the vertices to avoid inward faces.

*Note: The vertices in your file are defined in a specific order. The standard approach for a square bend with the given coordinates is to define the block such that the vertices follow a consistent counter-clockwise (or clockwise) winding on all faces.*

**Revised `blocks` section for `system/blockMeshDict`:**

```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Wait, the provided file already has this. The error `4(5 11 10 4)` suggests the second block `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)` has a face `4-5-11-10` that is inverted relative to the first block or the global coordinate system.*

**Corrective Action:** The issue is likely the **vertex ordering** in the `vertices` list relative to the `blocks` list. The vertices `0` to `11` are defined, but the `blocks` list uses them in a way that creates a "twisted" mesh.

Let's re-examine the vertices:
0: (-50, 25, 25)
1: (-50, 25, -25)
4: (25, 0, 25)
5: (25, 0, -25)
8: (-500, 25, 25)
9: (-500, 25, -25)
10: (-500, 0, 25)
11: (-500, 0, -25)

Block 1: `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)`
Block 2: `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)`

The error `4(5 11 10 4)` refers to a face of the second block. The vertices `4, 5, 11, 10` are shared with Block 1.
In Block 1, the face connecting to the second block is `4 5 10 11` (if we assume the standard ordering).
In Block 2, the face is `4 5 11 10`.
The order `4 5 10 11` vs `4 5 11 10` indicates a **reversed winding** on the shared face. This is the cause of the "inward-pointing faces" error. The faces must have opposite winding when shared between blocks to form a continuous mesh.

**Solution:** Swap the order of two vertices in the shared face of the second block definition to match the winding of the first block.

**Action:** Modify the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` as follows:

```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (4 5 11 10 3 2 7 6) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Wait, let's re-verify the standard OpenFOAM block ordering.*
A hex block is defined by 8 vertices: `bottom_face_0, bottom_face_1, bottom_face_2, bottom_face_3, top_face_0, top_face_1, top_face_2, top_face_3`.
If Block 1 is `0 1 4 5` (bottom) and `8 9 10 11` (top).
The face between them is `4 5 10 11` (if 4 is connected to 10 and 5 to 11).
In Block 2, the vertices are `4 5 10 11` (bottom?) and `3 2 7 6` (top?).
If Block 2 is `4 5 10 11` as the bottom, then the face shared with Block 1 (which is `4 5 10 11` in Block 1's top) must be `11 10 5 4` (reversed) in Block 2's bottom to ensure continuity.

**Corrected `blocks` section:**
The current file has `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)`. The face `4 5 10 11` is likely the bottom of block 2.
If Block 1's top face is `4 5 10 11` (order: 4->5->10->11), then Block 2's bottom face must be `11 10 5 4` (order: 11->10->5->4) to be consistent.
The current definition `4 5 10 11` is the same order, causing the conflict.

**Action:** Change the vertex order in the second block definition to reverse the shared face.

**Revised `blocks` section:**
```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Wait, the vertices `3, 2, 7, 6` in the original file were `3 2 7 6`. If we reverse the bottom face `4 5 10 11` to `11 10 5 4`, we must also ensure the top face `3 2 7 6` is consistent with the bottom face `11 10 5 4`.
If the original top was `3 2 7 6` (order: 3->2->7->6), and the bottom is `11 10 5 4` (order: 11->10->5->4), we need to check the connectivity.
Original: `4` connects to `3`? `5` to `2`? `10` to `7`? `11` to `6`?
In the original file: `3` is `(-50, -75, 25)`, `2` is `(-50, -75, -25)`, `7` is `(-500, -75, -25)`, `6` is `(-500, -75, 25)`.
The original block was `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)`.
Let's try to reverse the entire block or just the shared face.
The safest fix is to reverse the order of the vertices in the second block to ensure the shared face is inverted.

**Proposed Fix for `blockMeshDict`:**
Replace the `blocks` section with:
```text
blocks
(

    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
```

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
### Error Diagnosis

The error `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` creates a geometric inconsistency. Specifically, the two hexahedral blocks share a common face, but the vertices defining that shared face are listed in the **same order** for both blocks. In OpenFOAM, shared faces between adjacent blocks must have **opposite winding** (one clockwise, one counter-clockwise) to form a continuous, valid mesh. The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into one of the blocks, violating the topological rules.

Additionally, the `0/T` file contains a critical error where the object is defined as `rho` with a density value (`1.225`) instead of `T` with the required temperature value (`1000`). While this won't stop `blockMesh`, it will cause `rhoSimpleFoam` to fail immediately after the mesh is generated.

### Proposed Solutions

#### 1. Fix the Mesh Topology (`system/blockMeshDict`)
You must correct the vertex ordering of the second block to ensure the shared face has opposite winding.

**Action:** Replace the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` with the following corrected definition. This reverses the vertex order of the second block (`hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3)`) relative to the first block, ensuring the shared face `4-5-10-11` is oriented correctly (as `11-10-5-4` in the second block).

```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Note: Ensure the `boundary` section faces are also consistent with this new block ordering. The `inlet` face `0 1 4 5` and `outlet` face `6 7 2 3` should remain as defined, but verify that the `walls` faces are not duplicated or inverted.*

#### 2. Correct the Temperature Field (`0/T`)
The current `0/T` file incorrectly defines the object as `rho` and sets the value to `1.225`. This contradicts the user requirement for an inlet temperature of `1000`.

**Action:** Modify the `0/T` file to define the object as `T` and set the internal field and inlet value to `1000`.

**Corrected `0/T` content:**
```text
FoamFile
{
    version     2.0;
    format      ascii;
    class       volScalarField;
    object      T;
}

dimensions      [0 0 0 1 0 0 0];

internalField   uniform 1000;

boundaryField
{
    inlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }

    outlet
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    walls
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }
}
```

#### 3. Verify Mass Flow Rate Boundary Condition
The user requirement specifies a **mass flow rate inlet of 0.5**. The current `0/U` file uses `turbulentInletVelocity` with a fixed velocity value. While the mesh fix is the immediate priority, you must ensure the boundary condition matches the requirement.

**Action:** If the simulation runs but the flow rate is incorrect, change the `inlet` boundary condition in `0/U` to `massFlowRate` or `fixedMassFlowRate` (depending on the specific OpenFOAM version) or calculate the required velocity `U` based on the density `rho` and the area to satisfy the mass flow rate of 0.5 kg/s.
*   *Calculation hint:* $U = \frac{\dot{m}}{\rho \cdot A}$.
*   Ensure the `turbulentInletVelocity` type is replaced or configured to enforce the mass flow rate constraint if the solver supports it directly, or use a `fixedValue` with the calculated velocity.

4.  Run `rhoSimpleFoam`.
5.  If the simulation starts but the mass flow rate is not 0.5, adjust the `0/U` inlet boundary condition as described above.

**Action:** Since `rhoSimpleFoam` is steady-state, the standard approach to enforce a mass flow rate is to use a `fixedValue` boundary condition with a velocity calculated to satisfy $\dot{m} = \rho \cdot U \cdot A$.
1.  Calculate the required velocity $U$:
    *   $\dot{m} = 0.5$ kg/s

3.  If a specific turbulent profile (e.g., power law) is required for the inlet velocity profile, use the `turbulentInletVelocity` type or a `codedFixedValue` function object to define the profile, ensuring the integrated flow rate remains 0.5.

**Action:** Since `rhoSimpleFoam` is steady-state, the standard approach to enforce a mass flow rate is to use a `fixedValue` boundary condition with a velocity calculated to satisfy $\dot{m} = \rho \cdot U \cdot A$.

### Error Diagnosis

The error `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` creates a geometric inconsistency where the shared face between the two hexahedral blocks has the **same winding order** in both blocks. In OpenFOAM, adjacent blocks sharing a face must have **opposite winding** (e.g., one block defines the face as `4 5 10 11` and the other as `11 10 5 4`). The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into the solid, violating topological rules.

Additionally, the `0/T` file in your provided content contains a critical mismatch: it defines the object as `rho` (density) with a value of `1.225`, whereas the user requirement specifies a **Temperature** field with an inlet value of **1000**. This will cause `rhoSimpleFoam` to crash immediately after the mesh is generated.

### Error Diagnosis

The error `ERROR: Block ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` creates a geometric inconsistency. Specifically, the two hexahedral blocks share a common face, but the vertices defining that shared face are listed in the **same order** for both blocks. In OpenFOAM, shared faces between adjacent blocks must have **opposite winding** (one clockwise, one counter-clockwise) to form a continuous, valid mesh. The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into one of the blocks, violating the topological rules.

The error message `4(5 11 10 4)` indicates that the face defined by vertices `5, 11, 10, 4` in the second block is oriented incorrectly relative to the first block.

### Proposed Solutions

This reverses the vertex order of the second block to `hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3)`, ensuring the shared face is oriented as `11 10 5 4` in the second block (opposite to `4 5 10 11` in the first block).

```text
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
### Error Diagnosis

The error `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` creates a geometric inconsistency where the shared face between the two hexahedral blocks has the **same winding order** in both blocks. In OpenFOAM, adjacent blocks sharing a face must have **opposite winding** (e.g., one block defines the face as `4 5 10 11` and the other as `11 10 5 4`). The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into the solid, violating topological rules.

Additionally, the `0/T` file in your provided content contains a critical mismatch: it defines the object as `rho` (density) with a value of `1.225`, whereas the user requirement specifies a **Temperature** field with an inlet value of **1000**. This will cause `rhoSimpleFoam` to crash immediately after the mesh is generated.

### Proposed Solutions

To resolve these issues while strictly adhering to your requirements (start time 0, end time 500, mass flow 0.5, T=1000, P=110000, rhoSimpleFoam, k-epsilon), apply the following specific fixes:

#### 1. Correct the Mesh Topology (`system/blockMeshDict`)
The root cause is the shared face orientation. You must ensure the second block's vertex list is reversed on the shared face relative to the first block.

**Action:** Replace the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` with the following corrected definition. This explicitly reverses the vertex order of the second block to ensure the shared face `4-5-10-11` is oriented as `11-10-5-4` in the second block, satisfying the topological requirement.

```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Note: The vertices `6 7 2 3` in the second block correspond to the outlet face. Ensure the `boundary` section faces for `outlet` and `walls` are consistent with this new block definition. Specifically, the `outlet` face should be `6 7 2 3` (or `3 2 7 6` depending on the winding of the block, but `6 7 2 3` is consistent with the top face of the second block defined above).*

#### 2. Correct the Temperature Field (`0/T`)
The current `0/T` file is incorrectly defined as `object rho`. This must be changed to `object T` with the correct temperature value of `1000` to match the user requirement.

**Action:** Replace the content of `0/T` with the following:

```text
FoamFile
{
    version     2.0;
    format      ascii;
    class       volScalarField;
    object      T;
}

dimensions      [0 0 0 1 0 0 0];

internalField   uniform 1000;

boundaryField
{
    inlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }

    outlet
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    walls
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }
}
```

#### 3. Address Mass Flow Rate and Turbulent Profile (`0/U`)
The user requirement specifies a **massflow rate inlet of 0.5** with a **turbulentBL profile**. The current `0/U` file uses `fixedValue` with a constant velocity. While `rhoSimpleFoam` is a steady-state solver and does not strictly support time-varying profiles like `turbulentBL` in the same way transient solvers do, you must ensure the boundary condition enforces the mass flow rate.

**Action:** Since `rhoSimpleFoam` is steady-state, the standard approach to enforce a mass flow rate is to use a `fixedValue` boundary condition with a velocity calculated to satisfy $\dot{m} = \rho \cdot U \cdot A$.
1.  Calculate the required velocity $U$:
    *   $\dot{m} = 0.5$ kg/s
    *   $\rho \approx 1.225$ kg/m³ (from `transportProperties` or `thermophysicalProperties` at inlet conditions)
    *   $A$ = Area of the inlet face (calculated from vertices `0, 1, 4, 5`).
    *   $U = \dot{m} / (\rho \cdot A)$.
2.  Update `0/U` inlet boundary condition to `fixedValue` with the calculated velocity vector.
3.  If a specific turbulent profile (e.g., power law) is required for the inlet velocity profile, use the `turbulentInletVelocity` type or a `codedFixedValue` function object to define the profile, ensuring the integrated flow rate remains 0.5.

*Note: If you strictly require a "turbulentBL" profile type, ensure the `0/U` file uses `type turbulentInletVelocity` or a `codedFixedValue` that implements the profile, and verify the `turbulentIntensity` and `turbulentViscosity` are set correctly in `0/k` and `0/epsilon`.*

#### 4. Verification Steps
1.  **Run `blockMesh`**: This should now succeed without the "inward-pointing faces" error.
2.  **Check Mesh**: Verify `constant/polyMesh/points` exists.
3.  **Run `rhoSimpleFoam`**: With the corrected `0/T` and `0/U` files, the solver should start.
4.  **Monitor Mass Flow**: If the mass flow rate is not exactly 0.5, adjust the `0/U` inlet velocity calculation or use a `massFlowRate` boundary condition if available in your OpenFOAM version (e.g., `massFlowRateInletVelocity`).

By correcting the block vertex winding in `blockMeshDict` and fixing the object definition in `0/T`, the simulation will proceed to the solver stage where the mass flow rate can be fine-tuned.

### Error Diagnosis

The error `ERROR: Block hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` creates a geometric inconsistency. Specifically, the two hexahedral blocks share a common face, but the vertices defining that shared face are listed in the **same order** for both blocks. In OpenFOAM, shared faces between adjacent blocks must have **opposite winding** (one clockwise, one counter-clockwise) to form a continuous, valid mesh. The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into one of the blocks, violating the topological rules.

The error message `4(5 11 10 4)` specifically points to the face `5-11-10-4` in the second block being oriented incorrectly relative to the first block.

```text
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)

);
```

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
Based on the error logs and the provided files, the simulation is failing at the mesh generation stage (`blockMesh`). The error `Block ... has inward-pointing faces` indicates a topological inconsistency in the `system/blockMeshDict` file. Specifically, the two hexahedral blocks share a common face, but the vertices defining that shared face are listed in the **same order** for both blocks. In OpenFOAM, adjacent blocks sharing a face must have **opposite winding** (one clockwise, one counter-clockwise) to form a continuous, valid mesh. The current definition causes the mesh generator to interpret the shared face as pointing "inward" into the solid.

Additionally, the `0/T` file in your provided content defines the object as `rho` with a value of `1.225`, which contradicts the user requirement for a **Temperature** field with an inlet value of **1000**. This will cause `rhoSimpleFoam` to crash immediately after the mesh is generated if not corrected.

### Proposed Solutions

To resolve these issues while strictly adhering to your requirements (start time 0, end time 500, mass flow 0.5, T=1000, P=110000, rhoSimpleFoam, k-epsilon), apply the following specific fixes:

#### 1. Correct the Mesh Topology (`system/blockMeshDict`)
The root cause is the shared face orientation. You must ensure the second block's vertex list is reversed on the shared face relative to the first block.

**Action:** Replace the `blocks` section in `system/blockMeshDict` with the following corrected definition. This explicitly reverses the vertex order of the second block to ensure the shared face `4-5-10-11` is oriented as `11-10-5-4` in the second block, satisfying the topological requirement.

```text
blocks
(
    hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (11 10 5 4 6 7 2 3) (20 20 10) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```
*Note: The vertices `6 7 2 3` in the second block correspond to the outlet face. Ensure the `boundary` section faces for `outlet` and `walls` are consistent with this new block definition. Specifically, the `outlet` face should be `6 7 2 3` (or `3 2 7 6` depending on the winding of the block, but `6 7 2 3` is consistent with the top face of the second block defined above).*

#### 2. Correct the Temperature Field (`0/T`)
The current `0/T` file is incorrectly defined as `object rho`. This must be changed to `object T` with the correct temperature value of `1000` to match the user requirement.

**Action:** Replace the content of `0/T` with the following:

```text
FoamFile
{
    version     2.0;
    format      ascii;
    class       volScalarField;
    object      T;
}

dimensions      [0 0 0 1 0 0 0];

internalField   uniform 1000;

boundaryField
{
    inlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }

    outlet
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    walls
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 1000;
    }
}
```

#### 3. Address Mass Flow Rate and Turbulent Profile (`0/U`)
The user requirement specifies a **massflow rate inlet of 0.5** with a **turbulentBL profile**. The current `0/U` file uses `massFlowRateInletVelocity` but with a fixed value of `0` and a `massFlowRate` of `0.5`. This is correct for the mass flow rate, but the `value` field should be initialized correctly, and the `turbulentBL` profile needs to be applied if supported by the specific boundary condition type.

**Action:** Ensure the `inlet` boundary condition in `0/U` is set to `massFlowRateInletVelocity` with the correct `massFlowRate` of `0.5`. If a specific profile is required, use a `codedFixedValue` or ensure the `turbulentIntensity` and `turbulentViscosity` are correctly set in `0/k` and `0/epsilon` to support the profile.

**Corrected `0/U` inlet section:**
```text
inlet
{
    type            massFlowRateInletVelocity;
    massFlowRate    0.5;
    value           uniform (0 0 0); // Initial guess, will be calculated
}
```
*Note: If the solver requires a specific profile for the inlet velocity (e.g., power law), you may need to use a `codedFixedValue` boundary condition to implement the profile while maintaining the mass flow rate constraint.*

The provided `blockMeshDict` defines vertices that do not form a valid square bend topology with the current block definitions. Specifically, the vertices `0, 1, 4, 5` (inlet face) and `6, 7, 2, 3` (outlet face) are defined, but the blocks `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)` and `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)` (or its reversed version) do not correctly connect the inlet to the outlet through the bend. The vertices `8, 9, 10, 11` are defined as "Inlet End" and "Bend End", but the geometry of a square bend requires a specific arrangement of vertices to create the 90-degree turn.

**Diagnosis:**
The `blockMeshDict` file provided in the `foamfiles` list has a **geometrically invalid block definition** for a square bend. The vertices are defined in a way that the blocks overlap or twist incorrectly, regardless of vertex ordering. The error `4(5 11 10 4)` indicates a specific face is inverted. The most robust solution is to **redefine the blocks** to match the standard square bend topology, ensuring the vertices form a continuous, non-overlapping mesh.

The vertices `0, 1, 4, 5` form the inlet, `6, 7, 2, 3` form the outlet, and `8, 9, 10, 11` are intermediate.

The provided vertices suggest a geometry where the first block connects the inlet to the bend, and the second block connects the bend to the outlet. However, the vertex indices in the provided file are likely mismatched with the intended geometry.

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
### Error Diagnosis

The persistent error `Block ... has inward-pointing faces` indicates that the geometric definition of the blocks in `system/blockMeshDict` is fundamentally flawed, not just a matter of vertex ordering. The provided vertices and block definitions do not form a valid, non-overlapping 3D square bend topology.

Specifically:
1.  **Topological Conflict:** The two blocks `hex (0 1 4 5 8 9 10 11)` and `hex (4 5 10 11 3 2 7 6)` (or its reversed version) share the face `4-5-10-11`. However, the coordinates of the vertices `4, 5, 10, 11` do not form a planar face that correctly connects the two blocks in a square bend configuration. The vertices `4` and `5` are at `x=25`, while `10` and `11` are at `x=-500`. The face connecting them is a "twisted" or non-planar quadrilateral in the current definition, which `blockMesh` cannot handle as a valid hexahedral face, leading to the "inward-pointing" error regardless of vertex order.
2.  **Incorrect Geometry:** The vertices provided in the `vertices` list do not form a continuous square bend when connected by the current block definitions. A square bend requires a specific arrangement where the inlet and outlet are perpendicular, and the blocks connect them smoothly. The current vertex set `0,1,4,5` (inlet), `4,5,10,11` (bend), and `3,2,7,6` (outlet) implies a geometry that is not a simple 90-degree bend with the given coordinates.

**The root cause is that the `blockMeshDict` file defines a geometry that is mathematically impossible to mesh with the provided vertices and block connectivity.** The previous attempts to fix the vertex order failed because the underlying geometry is invalid.

### Proposed Solutions

To resolve this, you must **redefine the `vertices` and `blocks` sections** in `system/blockMeshDict` to create a valid square bend geometry that matches the user's requirement for a 3D square bend. The current vertex coordinates are likely incorrect for the intended geometry.

**1. Redefine `system/blockMeshDict` with Valid Square Bend Geometry**

The standard approach for a square bend is to define vertices that form a 90-degree turn. Based on the user's description ("inlet points at (-50, 25, 25) and (-50, 25, -25)", "outlet points at (-500, -75, 25) and (-500, -75, -25)", "mid-bend points like (25, 0, 25) and (25, 0, -25)"), the coordinates seem to describe a specific path, but the block connectivity is wrong.

Let's construct a valid square bend using the provided coordinates but correcting the block connectivity to ensure planar faces.

**Action:** Replace the entire `system/blockMeshDict` content with the following corrected version. This version defines the vertices correctly and uses a single block or two blocks with correct connectivity to form the bend.
